This is an extraordinarily complex healthcare regulatory due diligence request for a $425M acquisition of a skilled nursing facility operator. Let me parse the key requirements:

**Transaction**: Silver Oak Healthcare LLC acquiring Sunset Senior Living Group (12 SNFs across AZ/NV/CA) for $425M

**Major Risk Categories Identified**:
1. False Claims Act qui tam lawsuit ($58.7M-$77.2M exposure)
2. Special Focus Facility candidate (Orange County - termination risk $24.6M)
3. CMS proposed staffing minimums ($4.3M annual cost increase)
4. DPNA revenue losses ($1.53M FY2024)
5. Civil monetary penalties ($137K paid)
6. Low star ratings (1 facility 1-star, 3 facilities 2-stars)
7. High staff turnover ($3.5M annual recruitment)
8. CHOW approval delays

**Complexity Assessment**: This is CLEARLY a **COMPLEX** query requiring:
- Multiple entities (12 facilities across 3 states)
- Multiple domains (regulatory compliance, litigation, employment, tax, real estate, insurance)
- Due diligence transaction context
- Transaction value $425M = large deal

**Per Research Planning Protocol**, I must:
1. Create session directory with research plan
2. Deploy multiple specialists in parallel (4-8 for complex queries)
3. Execute validation phase (tiered)
4. Generate memorandum via section writers + synthesis

**Specialist Delegation Analysis**:

Based on the keyword triggers in the orchestrator instructions, I need:

1. **pharma-regulatory-analyst** - Triggered by "SNF", "Medicare Part A", "CMS", "Requirements for Participation", "survey deficiencies", "Five Star ratings", "DPNA", "CMPs", "SFF"
2. **case-law-analyst** - Triggered by "Martinez v. Sunset", "qui tam", "False Claims Act", "litigation", "wrongful discharge", "resident rights violations"


3. **employment-labor-analyst** - Triggered by the 1,850-person workforce, 85% turnover rate, WARN Act implications, staffing adequacy concerns, and wage increase requirements
4. **regulatory-rulemaking-analyst** - Triggered by 42 CFR Part 483 compliance gaps and the 2024 CMS staffing rule changes published in the Federal Register
5. **insurance-coverage-analyst** - Triggered by multiple liability exposures including the FCA claim, resident injury claims, and employment-related claims requiring assessment of general liability, directors & officers, and professional liability policies
6. **commercial-contracts-analyst** - Triggered by provider agreements, managed care contracts, and acquisition-related commercial arrangements that may contain change of control provisions
7. **financial-analyst** - Triggered by quantified exposures exceeding $1M (FCA exposure of $58.7M, SFF penalties of $24.6M, staffing-related costs of $4.3M) requiring risk aggregation modeling
8. **securities-researcher** - Triggered by the private equity sponsors (Golden Gate Capital and Silver Oak Healthcare) requiring SEC filing review to determine public debt obligations and reporting requirements

This is fundamentally an M&A due diligence engagement with multiple legal, regulatory, and financial risk domains requiring coordinated analysis across specialized expertise areas.

I need to establish a structured research framework starting with session initialization and systematic decomposition. The approach involves creating a session directory to organize outputs, then executing parallel specialist research with full domain coverage verification. For healthcare regulatory compliance specifically, I'm examining CMS participation requirements under 42 CFR Part 483, the Five Star Quality Rating System implications, Special Focus Facility designations, survey deficiency classifications, and payment denial consequences.

The False Claims Act litigation domain centers on the Martinez v. Sunset qui tam case with DOJ involvement, focusing on billing practice allegations including RUG-IV and PDPM coding issues, potential Anti-Kickback Statute breaches related to medical director arrangements, and settlement exposure including Corporate Integrity Agreement terms. Employment challenges span 1,850 staff across 12 locations with significant turnover rates—CNAs at 85%, LPNs at 55%, RNs at 40%—requiring workforce stability analysis.

Real estate considerations involve 8 owned and 4 leased facilities, with sale-leaseback options and Life Safety Code requirements affecting licensure. Tax structuring decisions between asset and stock purchases, Section 338(h)(10) elections, and multi-state implications (Arizona, Nevada, California) require careful planning. Insurance coverage gaps need assessment across professional liability for nursing care, general liability for resident incidents, and D&O protection against regulatory and litigation exposure.

The transaction involves multiple contractual layers: Medicare provider agreements across the network, medical director arrangements requiring fair market value validation, managed care relationships, and therapy service contracts. HIPAA compliance and business associate agreements are critical given resident medical records involved. Since Medicare and Medicaid function as government payers through provider agreements, these quasi-contractual relationships carry significant weight in the deal structure.

For specialist mapping, I need to be more precise about regulatory versus transactional expertise. The pharma-regulatory-analyst focuses on FDA matters—drug approvals and recalls—which doesn't align here. Instead, I should prioritize: a regulatory-rulemaking-analyst for CMS staffing requirements and Federal Register updates; an employment-labor-analyst for staffing compliance and wrongful termination exposure; a case-law-analyst for False Claims Act and resident rights litigation; an insurance-coverage-analyst to assess FCA and injury liability coverage; a commercial-contracts-analyst for medical director FMV analysis and provider agreement terms; a tax-structure-analyst for M&A structuring and Section 338 implications; a financial-analyst to model purchase price adjustments; and a securities-researcher if the PE sponsors have public company filings to review. The regulatory-rulemaking-analyst covers Federal Register and CFR rules, which includes CMS requirements in 42 CFR Part 483—so that's the appropriate specialist for nursing home compliance issues like Requirements for Participation, survey procedures, and enforcement actions. I should also check what specialized tools are available: CourtListener for the Martinez litigation, SEC filings for PE sponsor information, and potentially FDA tools, though those won't be directly relevant here.

The Federal Register will have CMS rulemaking on staffing standards, US Code contains the False Claims Act and Medicare statutory framework, and CourtListener provides access to the Martinez v. Sunset case. With those resources identified, I can structure the research plan around the key legal questions, starting with False Claims Act liability for the alleged therapy upcoding and unnecessary treatments during the 2019-2022 period.

For the qui tam action, I need to determine when DOJ might intervene in the Martinez case. CMS regulations on Special Focus Facility status create potential deal-blocking risks if Orange County Care Center can't demonstrate sustained improvement before full SFF designation. The proposed 2024 staffing minimums at 3.45 hours per patient day will trigger material compliance costs with a phase-in timeline I need to identify. Sunset's pattern of denial of payment for new admissions across facilities suggests systemic quality issues under the payment denial regulations. I should also examine the Medicare provider agreement termination provisions to assess the full scope of regulatory exposure.

The Change of Ownership process across the 12-facility portfolio presents timing risks around CMS Form 855A filing deadlines that could delay closing. Sunset's Five Star ratings—concentrated at 1 and 2-star facilities—create occupancy and reputational damage that should factor into purchase price adjustments. The medical director compensation structure at $10K-$15K monthly needs fair market value analysis under Anti-Kickback Statute standards. Finally, the 85% CNA turnover combined with the wrongful termination claim from Martinez represents significant labor exposure requiring quantified risk mitigation.
